text:
These are really good.  Being a kitchen soldier I had to modify the recipe just a bit. I increased the amount of bacon to 6 strips instead of 4 because bacon makes anything better.  I added a little olive oil and season all to the cabbage and onion while they were sauteing.  Everything else was done per the recipe. I think they have an aprodisiac kind of effect to them because my wife couldn't keep her hands off of me after I made these.  I made them with another recipe found here for meat loaf and it was just scrupious.  Hope you all enjoy my review and remember, don't let your meat loaf.

text:
For St. Patrick's Day 2004, I made this side dish to go with our corned beef.  I made it again today for this year's St. Patty's feast.  My family loves it.

The only thing I changed, following a reviewers suggestion, was to use a 16 oz. bag of cole slaw mix instead of the 1/2 head of cabbage.  It turned out great and I liked the little bit of color the carrot added.

This one's definitely a keeper.

text:
This was a hearty, warming vegetarian main dish for a cold evening. I omitted the bacon and subbed olive oil and butter to saute the cabbage mix and added 2 lg cloves of garlic to compensate for the flavor.  I boiled the potato in veggie broth for the same reason.  I also increased the relative proportions of cabbage and onion to potato.  Lastly, I added about a 1/4 c. or so of aged white cheddar with a little extra as garnish with more dill too.   Next time I will try carrots, turnips or rutabagas with the potato for a change of pace, or perhaps try some Guiness Stout instead of the milk for a vegan dish.

text:
Made this on St. Pat's Day when the family asked to try a traditional Irish dish.  The kids watched me making it, announced that it looked "strange" and said they would try just a little.  They loved it and wanted me to make it again a week later!  I used some baby yellow potatoes since that was what I had on hand & a bag of shredded cabbage for coleslaw.  The first time I used some liquid from my corned beef to sort of steam the cabbage rather than saute it, and the second time I prepared it following the recipe.  It was great either way.

text:
I still love making/eating this stuff and am so delighted that there are so many others who've enjoyed it over the years as well! Just thought I'd share a tip that I've come to love over the years... sometimes I forget to melt the butter used to pour into the well and when that happens I don't make a well but I simply cut the 1/4 cup butter into chunks and press them slightly into the surface of the colcannon. Within minutes there are multiple "mini wells" of melted buttery yumminess! Everybody gets to have a good shot at getting a serving with melted butter! Oh, and I've also started using more bacon! Life's too short not to! :-)

text:
Regarding the cabbage versus kale debate:  why not both?  Regarding the amount of bacon:  why not more?  I made this for the first time this year for St. Patrick's Day, and after reading the many comments, I decided to use both cabbage and kale.  I also decided to use more bacon than the recipe called for, because... well, you know... it's bacon!  It was delicious, and the whole family really loved it.  I have made it once since then, and plan on doing so many times in the future.  It was a wonderful complement to my own famous Guinness slow-cooked corned beef.  This will become a staple recipe in our household to replace traditional mashed spuds.  It'll give me a chance to show off my Irish heritage in future meals, even when it's not St. Patrick's Day!

text:
Making this was a lot of fun, and it's hard to mess it up. There are a lot of good variations you can try with this. The last time I made this, I added a whole half a pack of bacon, rather than just 4 slices (I find it easier to dice up the bacon with some kitchen scissors prior to cooking it), reduced the potatoes to about 1 1/2 to 2 lbs of diced red potatoes (with skins), and threw in more cabbage. I used some left over heavy cream instead of milk (sour cream works good too). You can also add in a half a cup of green onions and/or leeks instead of onion.

Phenomenal!! I did do a few things different. I upped the bacon as suggested as well as the onion. While the cabbage and onion were sauteing I added Nature's Own seasoning and plenty of black pepper and salt. text:
I love his recipe as it is, but I did make some changes the next time that I think made it more to my taste and have gotten rave reviews.  I prepped early: nuked a pound of turkey bacon and tore the slices apart (approx .75 inches) rather than crumble,  smashed the ptotaoes (red with skin on-lazy) and added enough milk to add some moisture,  added some minced garlic to the chopped onion (softened in a little oil)and put it all in a casserole dish. I baked it for approximately 30 minutes before serving.

I made this during Christmas, when I volunteered to bring an Irish dish to an international-themed potluck. I didn't make the 'butter well' as suggested, mixing the butter throughout the potatoes instead. I also used a peppered bacon, and even went high-calorie by keeping the bacon drippings in the recipe (my mother groaned in dieting agony when I mentioned this to her). I had to add more salt than called for, but this was still a very good recipe. My friends all loved it, and I still had some leftovers that tasted good for lunch at work.

text:
This is not just for St.P day; I made it for Xmas dinner and my family insists it should be a new tradition and I should make it every year. So good! 1/2 cabbage isn't an exact amount so I did equal parts cabbage to potato and it was a success! I used a lot of pepper and found the bacon was salty enough so didn't add much salt. I left the skin on the potato and don't have a masher so this was a chunky dish rather than mashed. I didn't bother with the pool of butter and, having never tried Colcannon before, it wasn't missed. It's a great way to trick the starchoholics into eating some leafy greens. I won't reserve this for St.P day or Xmas, I will make this all year round and recommend it highly.

text:
i first used this recipe a few years ago for our neighbourhood St. Patrick's Day Feast.  It is now a tradition on the Sunday Before, and it grows each year.  The only addition I have ever made is the addition of seasoning to all layers.  I salt the water the potatoes boil in, add a little Celtic Grey Salt  and ground mixed peppercorns to the Cabbage and Onions as they brown.  I use the seasoning bacon that you can sometimes find in the mega mart, it's ends and pieces, but works great.  I usually double this recipe, but this year will have to triple it.    This also works great with Fried Chicken, Roast Turkey and Pork Roast.  The only year I didn't make this was the year I had the Irish Stew.

You wouldnt try this if you didnt eat, or like, potatoes or cabbage, so dont expect it to be good if you also dont like or eat bacon. And dont rate the recipe after youve completely changed it. Go post your recipe and see how others like yours. And if you say youre a Chef and you frequently give poor ratings and bad reviews, you obviously a crappy chef and fail at making even simple things that everyone else has great success with. This was excellent colcannon. It has great flavour and is easy to make. You need to use all the ingredients because there arent many ingredients in it to begin with. Im not Irish, but my ex husband is and I still make this for him and my son on St. Patricks Day and quiche on Nee Years.

So, if you still consider it colcannon, after my changes, then this is the best colcannon, outside of Belfast!!

This was EXCELLENT. text:
My husband said that this was by far the best mashed potatoes he has ever eaten! I used finely chopped leeks sauteed with the cabbage (also finely chopped) instead of the onion. The leek and cabbage mixture was a little dry while sauteing in the small amount of bacon fat, so instead of adding more fat, I added a little whole milk to moisten while simmering. This worked very well to soften the vegetables. The addition of pepper at the end made a big difference to the taste. Salt was not necessary due to the bacon (I added more bacon than recommended)I fried the bacon until just before it started to crisp up, so it was still soft so that it blended with the other textures when stirred through.

I took this to an Irish-theme dinner party on Friday and it was a hit, with some tweaks:  I used 6 strips of bacon, with an additional 2 strips to crumble on top.  Added 2T minced garlic towards end of onion/cabbage step.  Definitely use a lid to cook onion/cabbage or cabbage stays too crunchy before it starts to brown.  Added 1/2C light sour cream when mashing potatoes.  Garnished with chives.  Without these changes, even with plenty of salt, this was a little bland.  But with them, it was delish!

Diane thank you for posting a colcannon recipe that did not involve boiling the meat or cabbage! unfortunately too many cooks are hell bent on boiling the flavor right out of their food, and adding bland on top of bland, and relying on salt to give it any amount of flavor whatsoever. when you saute the cabbage in the bacon drippings, it adds a heavenly layer of flavor and it is absolutely a joy on the taste buds. I made this side dish for a St. Patrick's day pot luck at work. It was an instant success!! I was complimented on how authentic and traditional it was and how good it tasted! It was really easy to make and it took just a little under an hour (sorry, I'm a beginners' cook). I did not use the raw cabbage, instead using half a bag of coleslaw mix and using only one onion. Needless to say, the dish was a total hit and I would definitely make it again. Thank you so much for sharing your recipe.

I hunted down this specific recipe a couple months back when I did a Dinner Theme night. I love mashed potatoes, but I wanted something a little different. When I mashed my potatoes, I mashed them with sour cream and butter and plenty of salt. I cut the cooked cabbage into bits and folded it into the mashed potatoes, to give it a variety of textures. My husband isn't a fan of cabbage but he raves about these potatoes and never fails to return for seconds or sometimes thirds. Thanks for sharing this recipe!

text:
Absolutely luscious...fabulous!  Per several suggestions, I upped the bacon to 6 slices and used a 14 oz. bag of prepared cole slaw mix (cabbage + carrots.) I sauteed the onions in the bacon grease about 3 minutes before adding the cabbage mix. Used 3 large russet potatoes and 2 medium yellow potatoes, so it was a bit more than 2-1/2 pounds.  Plus a bought a hand-masher just for this.  Worked well to prepare it right before our dinner guests arrived, and kept in a warming oven during cocktails.  This will certainly be a centerpiece dish to all future St. Patrick's Day dinners....plus extra times throughout the year.

text:
This recipe is perfect as is and is very easy to modify to your family's taste.  This was the third time I prepared this recipe and for my family's taste, we like it with more cabbage (about half of a large head in 3.5 lbs of potatoes), green onions instead of regular and no bacon, since we had it with braised corned beef (also on AR).  We have had with grilled salmon  and roast beef in the past and use the bacon, along with following the recommended cabbage amounts.  This is a great way to get non cabbage eaters to consume it without complaint!  Oh, and if I'm feeling lazy, I just throw the chopped cabbage into the microwave for a couple of minutes,  especially if I'm not using bacon.

text:
Pretty good! While I prefer Ashley's colcannon (fabulous colcannon, also on this site), this was decent nonetheless. When paired with a hearty stew, this makes an ordinary meal extra special. :) Having said this, I think I'll stick with Ashley's recipe. The addition of garlic and a few seasonings really takes her colcannon over the top. NOTE: You must STEAM your cabbage in order for it to cook thoroughly. I've never had any luck sauteing it (my cabbage always ends up a tad crunchy). Simply cover your skillet with a lid and cook for 10 minutes or so. This simple change makes all the difference, IMHO. Thanks for sharing your authentic recipe, Diane. This was super yummy served with Irish stew on St. Paddy's Day! :-)

text:
I changed the recipe a bit, and it came out as a 4-star rating.  However, if I had prepared it exactly as written, it probably would've been a 5!  I didn't peel my potatoes (I like the skin), I steamed the cabbage to make it healthier, and I didn't use any bacon because I didn't have any.  I also used green onions instead of regular and added them raw at the end (the residual heat cooked them a little bit while retaining their flavor).  I also only used 2 Tbsp butter, added cold at the end and stirred in so it would melt.  While it probably would've tasted better with more butter, it honestly probably also would've been fine without any butter at all.  If I make this again, I will try it with bacon, no butter and regular onions (although I think I'll still prefer the green onions).  I like how cheap and healthy this recipe can be.

Excellent dish. I've made this several times this year with our home-grown, early-season potatoes and cabbage. Delish. Salty and crunchy bacon. Sweet cabbage, Creamy, buttery potatoes. userID:
337534
Display Name:
Lisa Scott Provost
isPro:
False
followersCount:
58

113
favoritesCount:
535
recipesCount:

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/2403120.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is a hearty and extra-tasty take on mashed potatoes! Don't let anyone tell you they don't like cabbage, make it anyway - this is SO good. 

I made this for the first time for a St. Patrick's day work potluck, so rather than serving right away they spent some QT in a crockpot. Since that usually dries out potatoes, I added an additional 1/2 cup milk. I also added about 1/2 cup light sour cream, because I always make my mashed potatoes that way. To make life easier, I bought 1lb of finely shredded cabbage (much more fine than a regular slaw mix with red cabbage and carrots), and I cooked it and the onions until they were very soft and pretty darn caramelized. They both add a lot of veggie sweetness that way. 

I cooked and assembled the night before, then refrigerated the crock overnight; I added the butter in pats all over the top and lightly salted the whole thing before plugging in the slow cooker at work that morning. Worked perfectly! 

After crockpotting, the whole thing was a deep color, rather than the nice white photo here - but no one cared, it's so good! 

If I ever crockpot it again, I will wait to add the bacon until just before serving - it was tasty, but lost some zip and crunch after so much time hanging out in there. 

But for sure I will make this again. I'm glad I tried it, thanks for the recipe!
Review:
Rating:
5

Thought it was great.  I used turkey bacon but added some "real" bacon grease and a little olive oil, keeping the bacon in the pan when putting cabbage and onion to saute.  While potatoes boiled (skin-on yellow), the cabbage mixture simmered and wilted beautifully.  Don't forget the salt and pepper, it will need it.  Also, next time I would add cream cheese or sour cream to help with the texture as it was a little dense when mixed by hand.  Garlic would also help to boost flavor.
